# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-kubernetes`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-client-go`, `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes-api`, `github.com/sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd`

# Kubernetes Admission Webhook Processing Chain

## Your Task

Trace the admission webhook processing chain in Kubernetes. Find Go source files across kubernetes/kubernetes and kubernetes/api that implement: the generic Webhook dispatcher (in pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/), the mutating webhook dispatcher with reinvocation logic, the validating webhook dispatcher with parallel dispatch, the WebhookAccessor abstraction layer, and the MutatingWebhookConfiguration/ValidatingWebhookConfiguration API type definitions.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've successfully traced the Kubernetes admission webhook processing chain and created a comprehensive analysis. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified

**Abstraction Layer:**
- **WebhookAccessor** interface in `accessors.go` provides a unified abstraction for both mutating and validating webhooks

**Generic Dispatcher:**
- `webhook.go` in `generic/` implements the base admission plugin infrastructure
- `interfaces.go` defines the Dispatcher, Source, and WebhookInvocation contracts

**Mutating Webhooks:**
- `dispatcher.go` processes webhooks sequentially with sophisticated **reinvocation logic**
- `reinvocationcontext.go` tracks mutations and determines which webhooks need reinvocation
- `plugin.go` registers the "MutatingAdmissionWebhook" plugin

**Validating Webhooks:**
- `dispatcher.go` processes webhooks **in parallel** using goroutines for performance
- Caches versioned attributes to avoid redundant conversions
- `plugin.go` registers the "ValidatingAdmissionWebhook" plugin

**Configuration Management:**
- `mutating_webhook_manager.go` and `validating_webhook_manager.go` dynamically load webhook configs from Kubernetes API objects
- Use informers for real-time updates and lazy evaluation for caching

**API Types (in kubernetes-api):**
- `MutatingWebhookConfiguration` and `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration` cluster-scoped resources
- `MutatingWebhook` and `ValidatingWebhook` individual webhook definitions

The detailed findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbols, and a narrative explanation of the entire processing chain.

'*' is all groups.\\n27: \\t// If '*' is present, the length of the slice must be one.\\n28: \\t// Required.\\n29: \\t// +listType=atomic\\n30: \\tAPIGroups []string `json:\\\"apiGroups,omitempty\\\" protobuf:\\\"bytes,1,rep,name=apiGroups\\\"`\\n31: \\n32: \\t// APIVersions is the API versions the resources belong to. `json:\\\"apiVersions,omitempty\\\" protobuf:\\\"bytes,2,rep,name=apiVersions\\\"`\\n37: \\n38: \\t// Resources is a list of resources this rule applies to.\\n39: \\t//\\n40: \\t// For example:\\n41: \\t// 'pods' means pods.\\n42: \\t// 'pods/log' means the log subresource of pods.\\n43: \\t// '*' means all resources, but not subresources.\\n44: \\t// 'pods/*' means all subresources of pods.\\n45: \\t// '*/scale' means all scale subresources.\\n46: \\t// '*/*' means all resources and their subresources.\\n47: \\t//\\n48: \\t// If wildcard is present, the validation rule will ensure resources do not\\n49: \\t// overlap with each other.\\n50: \\t//\\n51: \\t// Depending on the enclosing object, subresources might not be allowed.\\n52: \\t// Required.\\n53: \\t// +listType=atomic\\n54: \\tResources []string `json:\\\"resources,omitempty\\\" protobuf:\\\"bytes,3,rep,name=resources\\\"`\\n55: \\n56: \\t// scope specifies the scope of this rule.\\n57: \\t// Valid values are \\\"Cluster\\\", \\\"Namespaced\\\", and \\\"*\\\"\\n58: \\t// \\\"Cluster\\\" means that only cluster-scoped resources will match this rule.\\n59: \\t// Namespace API objects are admission webhook processing chain is implemented through a coordinated system of components:\\n\\n## Architecture Overview\\n\\nThe admission webhook processing chain is a multi-layered system implemented in the kubernetes/kubernetes and kubernetes/api repositories. The chain processes both mutating webhooks (that can modify objects) and validating webhooks (that only validate objects).\\n\\n## Core Components\\n\\n### 1. WebhookAccessor Abstraction Layer\\nThe WebhookAccessor interface (defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/accessors.go`) provides a unified abstraction for accessing both MutatingWebhook and ValidatingWebhook objects. This interface implements the methods needed to support matching against webhook predicates, including GetUID, GetConfigurationName, GetRESTClient, GetCompiledMatcher, and various getter methods for webhook configuration fields.\\n\\nTwo concrete implementations are provided:\\n- `mutatingWebhookAccessor`: Wraps v1.MutatingWebhook objects\\n- `validatingWebhookAccessor`: Wraps v1.ValidatingWebhook objects\\n\\nBoth are instantiated via factory functions `NewMutatingWebhookAccessor` and `NewValidatingWebhookAccessor` respectively.\\n\\n### 2. Generic Webhook Dispatcher\\nThe generic webhook dispatcher (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/webhook.go`) is the abstract admission plugin that provides the infrastructure for both mutating and validating webhooks. The `Webhook` struct handles:\\n- Webhook configuration management through a `sourceFactory`\\n- Client connection management via `ClientManager`\\n- Predicate matching (namespace and object selectors)\\n- Delegation to specific mutating or validating dispatchers\\n\\nThe dispatcher interfaces are defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/generic/interfaces.go`, including the `Dispatcher` interface that handles actual webhook invocation.\\n\\n### 3. Mutating Webhook Dispatcher with Reinvocation Logic\\nThe mutating webhook dispatcher (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/dispatcher.go`) implements the `Dispatcher` interface and processes mutating webhooks sequentially. It includes sophisticated reinvocation logic:\\n\\n- Tracks previously invoked webhooks via `webhookReinvokeContext`\\n- Manages object mutations across multiple webhook invocations\\n- Detects when in-tree plugins have mutated the object and triggers webhook reinvocation\\n- Maintains state about which webhooks have been invoked and should be reinvoked\\n\\nThe reinvocation context (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/reinvocationcontext.go`) is a key component that:\\n- Tracks the last webhook output to detect changes\\n- Maintains sets of previously invoked reinvocable webhooks\\n- Manages which webhooks need to be reinvoked based on object mutations\\n\\nThe mutating webhook plugin (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/mutating/plugin.go`) registers itself as \\\"MutatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" and implements the admission.MutationInterface.\\n\\n### 4. Validating Webhook Dispatcher with Parallel Dispatch\\nThe validating webhook dispatcher (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/dispatcher.go`) processes validating webhooks in parallel for improved performance. Key features:\\n\\n- Constructs all necessary versions needed for webhook calls upfront\\n- Caches versioned attributes to avoid redundant conversions\\n- Spawns goroutines for each webhook invocation in parallel\\n- Aggregates errors from all webhooks\\n- Includes panic recovery mechanisms for webhook failures\\n\\nThe validating webhook plugin (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/plugin/webhook/validating/plugin.go`) registers itself as \\\"ValidatingAdmissionWebhook\\\" and implements the admission.ValidationInterface.\\n\\n### 5. Configuration Management\\nTwo configuration managers handle the dynamic loading and watching of webhook configurations:\\n\\n- `mutatingWebhookConfigurationManager` (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/mutating_webhook_manager.go`) manages MutatingWebhookConfiguration objects using informers and creates mutating webhook accessors\\n- `validatingWebhookConfigurationManager` (in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/admission/configuration/validating_webhook_manager.go`) manages ValidatingWebhookConfiguration objects similarly\\n\\nBoth managers implement the `generic.Source` interface and use lazy evaluation with cache invalidation on updates.\\n\\n### 6. API Type Definitions\\nThe webhook configuration types are defined in `admissionregistration/v1/types.go` in the kubernetes-api repository:\\n\\n- `MutatingWebhookConfiguration`: Cluster-scoped resource containing a list of MutatingWebhook definitions\\n- `ValidatingWebhookConfiguration`: Cluster-scoped resource containing a list of ValidatingWebhook definitions\\n- `MutatingWebhook`: Individual webhook configuration with name, client config, rules, and failure policy\\n- `ValidatingWebhook`: Individual webhook configuration for validation-only purposes\\n\\nThese types are registered in `admissionregistration/v1/register.go`.\\n\\n## Processing Chain Flow\\n\\n1. When a request arrives, the admission system invokes either the mutating or validating webhook plugin\\n2. The plugin delegates to the generic Webhook's Dispatch method\\n3. The generic webhook queries the configuration manager for active webhooks (wrapped as WebhookAccessor)\\n4. For each webhook, it evaluates predicates (rules, namespaceSelector, objectSelector) via ShouldCallHook\\n5. Matching webhooks are passed to the dispatcher (mutating or validating)\\n6. For mutating webhooks: Sequential processing with reinvocation logic tracks mutations\\n7. For validating webhooks: Parallel processing for performance with error aggregation\\n8. The final decision (allow/deny) and any mutations are returned to the API server\\n\\nThis architecture provides a flexible, extensible, and performant framework for dynamic admission webhooks in Kubernetes.\"\n}\n",
